blocks until the context is cancelled.\n42: \t// Run must ensure all goroutines are terminated before returning.\n43: \tRun(context.Context)\n44: }\n45: \n46: // ControllerConstructor is a constructor r.isCloudProviderController\n84: }\n85: \n86: // RequiresSpecialHandling should return true only in a special non-generic controllers like ServiceAccountTokenController\n87: func (r *ControllerDescriptor) RequiresSpecialHandling() bool {\n88: \treturn r.requiresSpecialHandling\n89: }\n90: \n91: // BuildController creates a controller based on the given descriptor.\n92: // The Overview\\n\\nKubernetes implements controller registration through a manager pattern defined in the kube-controller-manager. This architecture differs from the external controller-runtime library but follows similar principles.\\n\\n## Core Components\\n\\n### 1. Controller Interface (cmd/kube-controller-manager/app/controller_descriptor.go)\\n\\nThe fundamental interface that all controllers must implement:\\n```go\\ntype Controller interface {\\n  Name() string\\n  Run(context.Context)\\n}\\n```\\n\\nEvery controller registered with the manager must satisfy this interface with two methods:\\n- **Name()**: Returns the canonical name of the controller\\n- **Run(ctx context.Context)**: Executes the controller reconciliation loop; blocks until context is cancelled and ensures all goroutines are terminated before returning\\n\\n### 2. Controller Descriptor Pattern (cmd/kube-controller-manager/app/controller_descriptor.go)\\n\\nControllers are registered via descriptors that hold metadata and constructors:\\n```go\\ntype ControllerConstructor func(ctx context.Context, controllerContext ControllerContext, controllerName string) (Controller, error)\\n\\ntype ControllerDescriptor struct {\\n  name                      string\\n  constructor               ControllerConstructor\\n  requiredFeatureGates      []featuregate.Feature\\n  aliases                   []string\\n  isDisabledByDefault       bool\\n  isCloudProviderController bool\\n  requiresSpecialHandling   bool\\n}\\n\\nfunc (r *ControllerDescriptor) BuildController(ctx context.Context, controllerCtx ControllerContext) (Controller, error)\\n```\\n\\nThe **BuildController()** method (line 93) invokes the ControllerConstructor, which creates and returns the actual Controller implementation.\\n\\n### 3. Manager Registration Flow (cmd/kube-controller-manager/app/controllermanager.go)\\n\\nThe main entry point **Run()** function (line 185) orchestrates the controller lifecycle:\\n\\n1. **BuildControllers()** (line 256) - Creates all controllers from their descriptors:\\n   - Iterates through all ControllerDescriptors\\n   - Calls BuildController() for each descriptor\\n   - Collects controllers into a slice\\n   - Registers health checkers and debug handlers\\n\\n2. **RunControllers()** (line 271) - Starts all controllers concurrently:\\n   - Launches each controller in a separate goroutine\\n   - Applies jitter to stagger controller startup\\n   - Calls controller.Run(ctx) for each controller (line 722)\\n   - Manages shutdown gracefully with timeouts\\n\\n### 4. Controller Loop Wrapper (cmd/kube-controller-manager/app/controller_utils.go)\\n\\nThe **controllerLoop** struct wraps actual controller implementations to conform to the Controller interface:\\n```go\\ntype controllerLoop struct {\\n  name string\\n  run  runFunc\\n}\\n\\nfunc (loop *controllerLoop) Name() string {\\n  return loop.name\\n}\\n\\nfunc (loop *controllerLoop) Run(ctx context.Context) {\\n  loop.run(ctx)\\n}\\n```\\n\\nThe **newControllerLoop()** function creates these wrappers, turning any runFunc into a Controller.\\n\\n### 5. Concrete Example: Namespace Controller\\n\\n#### Constructor (pkg/controller/namespace/namespace_controller.go, line 66)\\n```go\\nfunc NewNamespaceController(\\n  ctx context.Context,\\n  kubeClient clientset.Interface,\\n  metadataClient metadata.Interface,\\n  discoverResourcesFn func() ([]*metav1.APIResourceList, error),\\n  namespaceInformer coreinformers.NamespaceInformer,\\n  resyncPeriod time.Duration,\\n  finalizerToken v1.FinalizerName) *NamespaceController\\n```\\n\\nCreates the actual NamespaceController struct with:\\n- A rate-limited work queue\\n- Informer event handlers for namespace changes\\n- A deletion handler for cleaning up namespace resources\\n\\n#### Reconciliation Loop (pkg/controller/namespace/namespace_controller.go, line 198)\\n```go\\nfunc (nm *NamespaceController) Run(ctx context.Context, workers int)\\n```\\n\\nThe Run method:\\n1. Waits for cache synchronization\\n2. Spawns worker goroutines\\n3. Each worker processes items from the queue indefinitely\\n4. Synchronizes namespace state and handles finalizers\\n5. Shuts down gracefully when context is cancelled\\n\\n#### Registration in Manager (cmd/kube-controller-manager/app/core.go, line 669-680)\\n\\nThe namespace controller is registered through:\\n```go\\nnamespaceController := namespacecontroller.NewNamespaceController(...)\\nreturn newControllerLoop(func(ctx context.Context) {\\n  namespaceController.Run(ctx, int(controllerContext.ComponentConfig.NamespaceController.ConcurrentNamespaceSyncs))\\n}, controllerName), nil\\n```\\n\\nThis wraps the domain-specific NamespaceController with its Run method into a generic controllerLoop implementing the Controller interface.\\n\\n## Extended Interfaces (staging/src/k8s.io/controller-manager/controller/interfaces.go)\\n\\nControllers can optionally implement additional interfaces:\\n\\n1. **Debuggable** - Provides HTTP debug handlers accessible at /debug/controllers/{controllerName}/\\n2. **HealthCheckable** - Enables custom health checks exposed on the /healthz endpoint\\n\\n## Registration Chain Summary\\n\\n1. kube-controller-manager starts (controllermanager.Run)\\n2. BuildControllers creates all registered controllers:\\n   - Invokes ControllerDescriptor.BuildController\\n   - Calls ControllerConstructor (e.g., newNamespaceController)\\n   - Wraps result in controllerLoop\\n3. RunControllers starts all controllers:\\n   - Spawns goroutine for each controller\\n   - Calls controller.Run(ctx)\\n   - Namespace controller processes work queue until context cancellation\\n4. Reconciliation loop continues until manager shutdown\\n\\nThis architecture separates domain-specific controller logic (pkg/controller/*) from manager infrastructure (cmd/kube-controller-manager/app), allowing clean composition and lifecycle management of multiple independent controllers within a single process.\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":4,"cache_creation_input_tokens":1163,"cache_read_input_tokens":98379,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":1163},"output_tokens":2,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"08b283e7-484c-4222-9b78-b5a32a1441dd","uuid":"66edd55e-3d6f-4c15-8984-14d93a80b665"}

Overview\\n\\nKubernetes implements controller registration through a manager pattern defined in the kube-controller-manager. This architecture differs from the external controller-runtime library but follows similar principles.\\n\\n## Core Components\\n\\n### 1. Controller Interface (cmd/kube-controller-manager/app/controller_descriptor.go)\\n\\nThe fundamental interface that all controllers must implement:\\n```go\\ntype Controller interface {\\n  Name() string\\n  Run(context.Context)\\n}\\n```\\n\\nEvery controller registered with the manager must satisfy this interface with two methods:\\n- **Name()**: Returns the canonical name of the controller\\n- **Run(ctx context.Context)**: Executes the controller reconciliation loop; blocks until context is cancelled and ensures all goroutines are terminated before returning\\n\\n### 2. Controller Descriptor Pattern (cmd/kube-controller-manager/app/controller_descriptor.go)\\n\\nControllers are registered via descriptors that hold metadata and constructors:\\n```go\\ntype ControllerConstructor func(ctx context.Context, controllerContext ControllerContext, controllerName string) (Controller, error)\\n\\ntype ControllerDescriptor struct {\\n  name                      string\\n  constructor               ControllerConstructor\\n  requiredFeatureGates      []featuregate.Feature\\n  aliases                   []string\\n  isDisabledByDefault       bool\\n  isCloudProviderController bool\\n  requiresSpecialHandling   bool\\n}\\n\\nfunc (r *ControllerDescriptor) BuildController(ctx context.Context, controllerCtx ControllerContext) (Controller, error)\\n```\\n\\nThe **BuildController()** method (line 93) invokes the ControllerConstructor, which creates and returns the actual Controller implementation.\\n\\n### 3. Manager Registration Flow (cmd/kube-controller-manager/app/controllermanager.go)\\n\\nThe main entry point **Run()** function (line 185) orchestrates the controller lifecycle:\\n\\n1. **BuildControllers()** (line 256) - Creates all controllers from their descriptors:\\n   - Iterates through all ControllerDescriptors\\n   - Calls BuildController() for each descriptor\\n   - Collects controllers into a slice\\n   - Registers health checkers and debug handlers\\n\\n2. **RunControllers()** (line 271) - Starts all controllers concurrently:\\n   - Launches each controller in a separate goroutine\\n   - Applies jitter to stagger controller startup\\n   - Calls controller.Run(ctx) for each controller (line 722)\\n   - Manages shutdown gracefully with timeouts\\n\\n### 4. Controller Loop Wrapper (cmd/kube-controller-manager/app/controller_utils.go)\\n\\nThe **controllerLoop** struct wraps actual controller implementations to conform to the Controller interface:\\n```go\\ntype controllerLoop struct {\\n  name string\\n  run  runFunc\\n}\\n\\nfunc (loop *controllerLoop) Name() string {\\n  return loop.name\\n}\\n\\nfunc (loop *controllerLoop) Run(ctx context.Context) {\\n  loop.run(ctx)\\n}\\n```\\n\\nThe **newControllerLoop()** function creates these wrappers, turning any runFunc into a Controller.\\n\\n### 5. Concrete Example: Namespace Controller\\n\\n#### Constructor (pkg/controller/namespace/namespace_controller.go, line 66)\\n```go\\nfunc NewNamespaceController(\\n  ctx context.Context,\\n  kubeClient clientset.Interface,\\n  metadataClient metadata.Interface,\\n  discoverResourcesFn func() ([]*metav1.APIResourceList, error),\\n  namespaceInformer coreinformers.NamespaceInformer,\\n  resyncPeriod time.Duration,\\n  finalizerToken v1.FinalizerName) *NamespaceController\\n```\\n\\nCreates the actual NamespaceController struct with:\\n- A rate-limited work queue\\n- Informer event handlers for namespace changes\\n- A deletion handler for cleaning up namespace resources\\n\\n#### Reconciliation Loop (pkg/controller/namespace/namespace_controller.go, line 198)\\n```go\\nfunc (nm *NamespaceController) Run(ctx context.Context, workers int)\\n```\\n\\nThe Run method:\\n1. Waits for cache synchronization\\n2. Spawns worker goroutines\\n3. Each worker processes items from the queue indefinitely\\n4. Synchronizes namespace state and handles finalizers\\n5. Shuts down gracefully when context is cancelled\\n\\n#### Registration in Manager (cmd/kube-controller-manager/app/core.go, line 669-680)\\n\\nThe namespace controller is registered through:\\n```go\\nnamespaceController := namespacecontroller.NewNamespaceController(...)\\nreturn newControllerLoop(func(ctx context.Context) {\\n  namespaceController.Run(ctx, int(controllerContext.ComponentConfig.NamespaceController.ConcurrentNamespaceSyncs))\\n}, controllerName), nil\\n```\\n\\nThis wraps the domain-specific NamespaceController with its Run method into a generic controllerLoop implementing the Controller interface.\\n\\n## Extended Interfaces (staging/src/k8s.io/controller-manager/controller/interfaces.go)\\n\\nControllers can optionally implement additional interfaces:\\n\\n1. **Debuggable** - Provides HTTP debug handlers accessible at /debug/controllers/{controllerName}/\\n2. **HealthCheckable** - Enables custom health checks exposed on the /healthz endpoint\\n\\n## Registration Chain Summary\\n\\n1. kube-controller-manager starts (controllermanager.Run)\\n2. BuildControllers creates all registered controllers:\\n   - Invokes ControllerDescriptor.BuildController\\n   - Calls ControllerConstructor (e.g., newNamespaceController)\\n   - Wraps result in controllerLoop\\n3. RunControllers starts all controllers:\\n   - Spawns goroutine for each controller\\n   - Calls controller.Run(ctx)\\n   - Namespace controller processes work queue until context cancellation\\n4. Reconciliation loop continues until manager shutdown\\n\\nThis architecture separates domain-specific controller logic (pkg/controller/*) from manager infrastructure (cmd/kube-controller-manager/app), allowing clean composition and lifecycle management of multiple independent controllers within a single process.\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
